I was pleasantly surprised how well this stuff works. The bottle is small, but you only use a few drops with each shave. And when they say a few drops, they *mean* a few drops. People who have had problems with gunking up the razor or poor performance, I suspect used too much oil - I did too the first time and received poor results. Once I cut pack and just used 2 drops in each palm, I got better gliding and no razor gunking up. It does give quite a close shave, and is a pleasant smell (unless you don't like clove/menthol-y smelling things). You do have to be religious about keeping the area wet as you shave, as the water is what helps it stay slick; if you don't, it will start to drag. Another small downside (or rather something to get used to) is that since there is no lather, it's a bit harder to tell where you've gone over and where you've missed. I have heard this stuff works great when adding a drop to regular lather, but honestly I've been fine with it by itself. It seems to help with razor burn a bit. I don't generally use aftershave with it, since it smells nice and does the job on it's own. I hate to say it, since I like it so much, but I'll probably be using it instead of my brush set for daily use. Overall, very glad I tried it, and I highly recommend it.

What do I mean by \\"too thick?\\" If an oil causes the razor to drag, then it is way too thick. This oil caused my razor to drag horribly and that is not a good thing when using a straight razor.<br /><br />Another large problem I have with Shave Secret is that I could not use the oil by itself and get a good shave out of it. As I pointed out, it became tacky on my skin, which caused razor drag and also meant that I wasn't getting a smooth shave. I used the oil on my final razor pass, without soap, and the oil caused more resistance than if I had dry shaved! I also tried using the oil with my shave soaps and the oil added nothing to the quality of my shave. What the oil does is allow the razor, whether it be foil or blade, to glide smoothly on the skin. Since the hairs are lubricated, the foil can simply glide over without pulling. This is important because you do not always get all of the hair in one pass. Typically, the ones that evade the blade gets pulled as the razor moves past, causing skin irritation and possible breakouts. You can then go back over the same area to get the remaining hairs. The oil allows you to do this, to do multiple passes over the same area, without razor burn.<br /><br />Use this product sparingly. You only need a few drops. Perhaps the best routine is to shave prior to taking your morning shower. That way, the oil gets washed away. The oil is supposedly good for your skin. I also ended up cutting myself two or three times every time I shaved. I put the whole works in a drawer when Harry came along in an e-mail offering a beautifully designed $15 dollar razor and German-made four-blade refill cartridge that cost wa-a-a-y-y less than Schick, Gillette, or Wilkinson Sword Competitors. The packaging was beautiful, the price was right, the flexible head on the Harry's razor comfortably followed the contours of my face and I thought I was finally there. I just have to be a little more careful that I don't miss any parts of my now amazingly smooth visage.
